Links: http://rd8hp6du2b.search.serialssolutions.com/directLink?&amp;atitle=PUBLIC+FORUM+SOBOROFF%27S+DEDICATION+NOT+JUST+PAR+FOR+COURSE&amp;author=&amp;issn=&amp;title=Daily+News&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;date=1997-08-06&amp;spage=N.12&amp;id=doi:&amp;sid=ProQ_ss&amp;genre=article

Full text: Letters to the Editor
Rick Orlov's (July 28) article on Steve Soboroff pointed out the many sides of this man. He is amazing.
As the president of the Recreation and Parks Commission, the fact he personally visited the 375 parks in the city should give you an idea of just how dedicated he has been as a commissioner.
I doubt in all the years this commission has existed that anyone has ever taken the time to do what Soboroff has done. He is unique because he gets down in the trenches and finds out for himself what this city is doing and what the local residents wish the city were doing.
He takes a look at what the public is complaining about and generally finds a solution that everyone can live with, then most important of all, he makes sure it gets done.
Soboroff was instrumental in starting a Golf Task Force along with Leroy Chase shortly after they became members of the commission. We are starting our second year of being a Golf Advisory Committee made up of representatives of the Men and Women's Municipal Golf Courses, the golf concessionaires and the Men and Women's Public Links Associations.
It is gratifying to see our input taken seriously by the department. Without Soboroff this may never have happened.
Thank you Rick Orlov for letting the people of Los Angeles know what a gem we have in this man. And thank you, Steve Soboroff, for all your hard work.
Lory Oberg
Vice chair
Los Angeles Recreation and Parks Golf Advisory Committee
Informing misinformed
William O. Felsman (Forum, July 30) concludes that "global warming is a scam based upon junk science" promoted by "the same folks who touted the imminent ice age and acid rain" and other "nonexistent environmental calamities."
Actually, acid rain still is recognized by a consensus of atmospheric scientists as a problem which causes fish kills and deforestation. Geologists still claim that there was an ice age (the Pleistocene Epoch) that ended 10,000 years ago. Further, the years 1550-1850 are known as the Little Ice Age, a period when glaciers again crept forward. This period ended, notably enough, when the Industrial Revolution led to a large increase in the burning of fossil fuels.
It is the burning of fossil fuels, coupled with deforestation (most of it not from acid rain) that is causing the build-up of carbon dioxide mainly responsible for global warming.
Felsman is so misinformed that he thinks the argument is that carbon dioxide is generating heat. He says that only the sun heats the Earth. Actually, carbon dioxide traps heat from the sun that would otherwise escape by infrared radiation.
He thinks that those who warn us about global warming are lying in order to seize political power, though he does not explain this peculiar notion. Who is warning us? The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change is an international network of 2,500 scientists specializing in climate study which has issued at least two reports (1990 and 1992) concluding that global warming by man-made sources has already begun, and that "greenhouse" gasses are "substantially increasing" ("Climate Change: The IPCC Scientific Assessment, 1990").
The National Academy of Sciences, in Policy Implications of Greenhouse Warming (1992), states that "greenhouse warming poses a potential threat sufficient to merit prompt responses."
A November 1991 Gallup Poll found that 66 percent of research scientists thought that human-induced global warming had already begun. Most of the rest were undecided whether it had started, but only 2 percent of those polled disagreed that substantial warming would occur over the next 50 to 100 years.
Felsman says that our future is too important to be delegated to "naked, would-be emperors." Well, neither should it be guided by the badly uninformed.
- Wayne J. Grabert
Chatsworth
Zacarias from same mold
In a July 3 article by Daily News Staff Writer Terri Hardy, ("LAUSD superintendent gives posts, raises to three aides"), it is quite obviously demonstrated that Ruben Zacarias is truly a product of the environment that spawned him.
The LAUSD always has had a penchant for throwing money at problems. The rub is that the problems keep getting worse and the amount of money is always increasing.
Zacarias is true to form in awarding a group of aides salary increases as high as 39 percent. That is the crux of the problem. Awarding overlords of a failed system massive salary increases is like giving the crew of the Titanic big raises for doing a good job.
Even Jeff Horton voted against the increases - the same Jeff Horton whose first official act as president of the school board was to award Board of Education employees "live in" coverage on their insurance, a gift to the homosexual community of which he is admittedly a member.
When that chicken comes home to roost, we taxpayers will be coughing up millions for AIDS-related disabilities alone.
It has become painfully clear that antiquated business and personnel practices, in concert with unprincipled unions, are about to sink our "Titanic."
I hope there is a Peter Ueberroth in our future, unfettered by the bureaucracies that caused him to resign his previous Los Angeles assignment, a real businessman who could assure a dollar of learning for every dollar spent. I'm sure, under his guidance, Zacarias' aides would be told to earn their present salaries or get out. After all, the 1984 Olympics was the most successful of all time. We could have the most successful school system of all time.
We must get rid of the entrenched bureaucrats, below-standard teachers and the tenure system, and our schools will thrive. Where are you, Peter Ueberroth?
- H.L. Bradbury
Granada Hills
As the parent of three school-age children, I am absolutely outraged at Ruben Zacarias' first great move as superintendent of the LAUSD. To promote and give pay increases of up to 39 percent to three staff members for any reason whatsoever only shows that it will be business as usual for our school district.
This nonsense about freeing himself to work on student performance is ridiculous. What is needed is to get the money out of the ivory tower and into the classrooms.
Zacarias apparently has no concerns about spending the money this way as the school board is more interested in giving him, their "breath of fresh air," what he wants than in what is best for our children.
Like many families, we pay taxes and private school tuition. I certainly resent the fact that I must continue to support a school district that is unable to provide an education for my children.
- Vicki Van Camp
Sylmar
Sorority off base
I just read a letter from Binnie Petty, representing the Beta Pi Sigma sorority, regarding CSUN President Blenda Wilson. I agree with Petty that there has been a tremendous amount of press given to Wilson's decision to eliminate four of CSUN's sports programs.
I also agree that academics is the primary charter at any university and that the athletic programs are secondary.
However, beyond those two points, Petty and her sorority sisters lose total credibility.
Her position is that the letter-writing public and the Daily News have been "spewing furor" and that Wilson has been "attacked and smeared more like a politician" over her decision to "implement gender equity."
The fact that there has been such a public outcry over this decision is a clear indication that something is terribly wrong here, and it has nothing to do with academics vs. athletics. It has everything to do with an unjust and prejudicial action taken by a public official.
Equity in funding between men's and women's sports is a good thing, and I wholeheartedly support it. It is not only the fair thing to do, the improvement our women have shown in international sports competition since the enactment of Title IX proves that it has had an immediate and positive effect.
The problem at CSUN is not that gender equity has been established. The problem is how Wilson chose to solve the $900,000 fiscal shortfall that resulted from enacting those measures. Had she decided to delete the soccer, volleyball, baseball/softball and swimming programs in their entirety at CSUN, there would not have been such a negative public outcry. It would have been seen as a tough but necessary decision.
However, Wilson did not do that.
Petty's position seems to be that Wilson is somehow immune from public scrutiny and should not be held accountable for her actions. While Wilson is not an elected official of California, she is an employee of the state and at some level has a responsibility to its taxpayers.
As with many special-interest groups today, Petty and her sorority sisters have allowed themselves to blindly support the inappropriate actions of an individual that their organization champions.
I choose to deplore the actions taken by Blenda Wilson. I am pleased to see that she has recently made herself available for the top position at another university outside of California. I wish her the best of luck in obtaining that position.
- Greg Davies
CSUN alumnus
Northridge
Terrorism won't go away
By now it has become clear that acts of terrorism are not about to cease in the Middle East. It is clear that no matter what sort of peace is eventually carved out, some radical group or another will be displeased, and that displeasure will lead to moIre cowardly acts on innocent civilians and tourists, as well as military and governmental personnel. It seems that since this is the case, the best solution to terrorism is to do exactly the opposite of what the terrorists demand.
Given the religious nature of the clash of ideologies in the Middle East, the Israel-Palestinian conflict will lead either to an uneasy peace or to war. War kills vastly more people than singular acts of terrorism, so why let this most recent bombing in Israel achieve its goal of hamstringing the already-stalled peace talks? Perhaps a brief period of suspension, out of respect to the killed or injured, seems appropriate, but even this doesn't effect any progress toward peace. Certainly, human emotions like anger and grief come into play, but if I were to die in a terrorist attack, I would not want my death to lead to intransigence of war. I would want my death to led to a stepping-up of negotiations, a more committed attempt to establish a compromise that both sides can find acceptable. Otherwise, won't more innocent people wind up following me, or worse, won't millions suffer in a devastating war?
- George Scileppi
Glendale

Full text: INTERNATIONAL A3-7
North Koreans Pushed To Starvation, Officials SayTwo months of high temperatures and no rain in North Korea have pushed millions of people in the isolated country, whose food stocks were already low, to the brink of famine, reported relief officials returning from recent visits there. A1

Oil Giant Adopts New StanceDelegates to a meeting on climate change in Bonn were surprised to hear British Petroleum, the world's third-largest oil company, announce that it believed that concern about the burning of fossil fuels was scientifically warranted. Industry lobbyists had previously denied a link between greenhouse gases and climate change. A1

Yeltsin Revalues the RubleRussians cynically watched tycoons and bankers feud over the privatization of a nickel mine, but reacted when President Boris N. Yeltsin announced that as of Jan. 1, his government will redenominate the ruble by a factor of 1,000. The move was meant to counter a symbol of inflation, which has led to the current exchange rate of 6,000 rubles to the dollar. Mr. Yeltsin, speaking while on holiday at a health spa, sought to assure wary Russians that the reform would ''not be a confiscation.'' People have until the end of the century to exchange their old bills. A3

U.S. Suspends Bosnia ContactThe Clinton Administration announced it would suspend its contacts with Bosnia's Ambassador to the United States. The major European countries have done the same, after Bosnia's three-member presidency in Sarajevo failed to agree upon and name ambassadors capable of representing Bosnia's Muslims, Croats and Serbs. Agreeing upon the diplomatic appointments was required by the Dayton peace accords that ended the civil war. A3

Israel Halts Revenue TransferThe Israeli Government suspended reimbursement of taxes and other fees owed to the Palestinian Authority. The fees account for the majority of the Palestinian Authority's annual revenue and represent a variety of taxes collected by Israel from Palestinians. Israeli officials acknowledged that the tactic violated the peace accord but said the funding could be restored if Palestinian leader Yasir Arafat and his Government begin to crack down on Islamic militants. A8

74 Killed in Algerian MassacresA total of 74 Algerian villagers were killed in a new series of massacres in the Blida and Ain-Defla regions, local residents said. The killings occurred within hours of a call by President Liamine Zeroual for public ''vigilance'' in the wake of a series of bloody massacres attributed to Islamic extremists that have left more than 600 dead in the last two months. NATIONAL A12-17
Panel Proposes Abolishing U.S. Immigration AgencyA Federal advisory panel has decided to recommend abolishing the embattled Immigration and Naturalization Service and assign its duties to other Government agencies in an effort to improve the nation's immigration system. The United States Commission on Immigration Reform is proposing that the Justice Department, the immigration service's parent agency, retain responsibility for controlling the border and removing illegal immigrants. The State Department, which now deals with visas at American embassies overseas, would handle immigration services and benefits, like citizenship requests. And the Labor Department, which now monitors wage and hour laws, would also enforce rules covering the hiring of foreign workers. A1

Medicare Poised for ReformThe budget bill awaiting President Clinton's signature includes two new health insurance options that give Medicare beneficiaries greater freedom to choose their doctors and hospitals, but it also exposes elderly patients to much higher costs. The options, which represent a radical departure from current Medicare policy, are likely to appeal to rugged individualists who resent Government interference with their medical care and can afford to pay more for it. A1

Title: News Summary:   [Summary ]

Publication title: New York Times, Late Edition (East Coast); New York, N.Y.
